## Finally! A pair of affordable Thunderbolt docks on Black Friday
 - [https://www.pcworld.com/article/1394947/finally-a-pair-of-affordable-thunderbolt-docks-on-black-friday.html](https://www.pcworld.com/article/1394947/finally-a-pair-of-affordable-thunderbolt-docks-on-black-friday.html)
 - RSS feed: https://www.pcworld.com/index.rss
 - date published: 2022-11-25 20:43:09+00:00
 - Starred: False

<div id="link_wrapped_content">
<section class="wp-block-bigbite-multi-title"><div class="container"></div></section><p>It can be difficult to find an inexpensive Thunderbolt dock, but this Black Friday offers two that we think are worth buying: the $216 Cable Matters 14-in-1 Thunderbolt Dock and the $159 Plugable 13-in-1 USB-C Docking Station.</p>



<p>Technically, the latter <a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://www.amazon.com/Plugable-Charging-DisplayPort-Compatible-Thunderbolt/dp/B09TQY97M&amp;xcust=2-2-1394947-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow">Plugable 13-in-1 USB-C dock</a> uses the <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/801587/why-new-usb-c-displaylink-docks-are-better-and-worse-than-thunderbolt.html">DisplayLink protocol</a>, a USB-C dock that uses compression to approximate the performance of a Thunderbolt dock. But we&rsquo;ve been impressed with the performance of DisplayLink docks across a variety of products, including Plugable&rsquo;s own products. We haven&rsquo;t yet reviewed the Plugable 13-in-1 USB-C docking station, but we&rsquo;re confident that it should live up to the standards that have helped Plugable products reach the top of our list of the <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/393714/best-thunderbolt-docks-for-a-laptop-pc.html">best Thunderbolt docks</a>. Unfortunately, many of those are priced well north of $300, and even close to $400.</p>



<p>What we like most about both the Plugable as well as the <a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://www.amazon.com/Cable-Matters-107044-Computer-Stations/dp/B08L9TCY25/&amp;xcust=2-2-1394947-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow">Cable Matters Hybrid 14-in-1 Dock</a> is that both manufacturers believe in a variety of display ports. HDMI? DisplayPort? No problem. Both docks include options for both display ports, <em>and</em> for both monitors. That&rsquo;s terrific flexibility, and even better news if you&rsquo;re buying these docks as a gift &mdash; whoever receives it won&rsquo;t have to buy an additional dongle or worry about which cable goes where.</p>



<p>Both of these docks offers substantial charging options, too. The Cable Matters dock supplies a rated 96W, and the Plugable dock provides 100W. That&rsquo;s more than enough for most USB-C powered laptops, though some recent gaming laptops may be an exception. Otherwise, you&rsquo;ll find a vast variety of ports that should accommodate legacy devices. Both docks are 36 percent off. Great prices, great docks: a solid Black Friday deal.</p>


<p class="cta wp-block wp-block-button"><a class="cta__btn" href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/1394947/finally-a-pair-of-affordable-thunderbolt-docks-on-black-friday.html" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">See the Plugable 13-in-1 USB-C Docking Station on Amazon for $159.20</a></p>

<p class="cta wp-block wp-block-button"><a class="cta__btn" href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://www.amazon.com/Cable-Matters-107044-Computer-Stations/dp/B08L9TCY25/&amp;xcust=2-2-1394947-7-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">See the Cable Matters 14-in-1 Thunderbolt Dock on Amazon for $215.99</a></p>

## Simplify your chores with this $99 Black Friday special on a robot vacuum
 - [https://www.pcworld.com/article/1394891/simplify-chores-with-this-99-dollar-black-friday-deal-on-a-eufy-robot-vacuum.html](https://www.pcworld.com/article/1394891/simplify-chores-with-this-99-dollar-black-friday-deal-on-a-eufy-robot-vacuum.html)
 - RSS feed: https://www.pcworld.com/index.rss
 - date published: 2022-11-25 19:08:08+00:00
 - Starred: False

<div id="link_wrapped_content">
<section class="wp-block-bigbite-multi-title"><div class="container"></div></section><p>Our robot overlords are supposed to <a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Terminator&amp;xcust=2-1-1394891-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow">rise against us</a> in several years, but until then, we can benefit their cleaning help. And right now, that assistance is cheaper than ever, thanks to a Walmart Black Friday deal on the <a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://www.walmart.com/ip/Anker-eufy-25C-Wi-Fi-Connected-Robot-Vacuum-Great-for-Picking-up-Pet-Hairs-Quiet-Slim/400599921&amp;xcust=2-1-1394891-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow">Anker eufy 25C Wi-Fi Robot Vacuum</a>. You can grab it for an ultra affordable $99, or a whopping 60 percent off.</p>



<p>This basic model handles just vacuuming, unlike much more expensive options that also do mopping. But for the price, this quiet little bot does a lot. It run up to 100 minutes at a time, and will automatically return to its base to recharge. It accepts commands by touch, from the companion smartphone app, or even your voice if you have an Alexa or Google Home compatible device. It even knows how to avoid falling down stairs.</p>



<p>The main &ldquo;issue&rdquo; with the eufy 25C is that it performs better on hard surfaces (e.g., wood floors) and as a budget vacuum, its navigation system isn&rsquo;t as sophisticated. You also have to clean it more frequently.</p>



<p>But for this stupendously low sale price, those are quibbles you could easily forgive. In exchange, you&rsquo;ll get a friendly assist with light cleaning to keep dust and dirt to minimum in between your deeper cleans. And it&rsquo;ll never shirk its duties or forget, either. At least, not until it joins a robot uprising.</p>

## This is the best Chromebook under $100 to buy on Black Friday
 - [https://www.pcworld.com/article/1394796/this-is-the-best-chromebook-under-100-to-buy-on-black-friday.html](https://www.pcworld.com/article/1394796/this-is-the-best-chromebook-under-100-to-buy-on-black-friday.html)
 - RSS feed: https://www.pcworld.com/index.rss
 - date published: 2022-11-25 18:38:17+00:00
 - Starred: False

<div id="link_wrapped_content">
<section class="wp-block-bigbite-multi-title"><div class="container"></div></section><p>The best Chromebook under $100 to buy on Black Friday is the Lenovo Chromebook 3 11.6-inch on sale for $79 at Best Buy. It&rsquo;s a decent machine with acceptable compromises.</p>



<p>The <a href="https://shop-links.co/link/?url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.bestbuy.com%2Fsite%2Flenovo-chromebook-3-11-6-hd-laptop-celeron-n4020-4gb-memory-64gb-emmc-onyx-black%2F6500335.p&amp;publisher_slug=pcworld&amp;exclusive=1&amp;article_name=pcworld&amp;article_url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.pcworld.com%2Ffeed" rel="nofollow">$79 Lenovo Chromebook 3 (normally $139.00) at Best Buy</a> doesn&rsquo;t offer the flashiest discount, but it has the best combination of features that avoids the pitfalls that other retailers offer. It&rsquo;s one of the leading offers on our list of <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/1383937/black-friday-chromebook-deals-nov-25.html">the best Chromebook deals of Black Friday</a>, which also includes higher-priced but more full-featured options.</p>



<p>We prioritize 8GB of RAM, a large, detailed screen, and a relatively fast processor as the key attributes for a Chromebook. At under $100, these are rare. Lenovo&rsquo;s Chromebook 3 offers just 4GB of RAM and an 11-inch, 768p screen. But for the price, these are acceptable steps down. We also like the fact that the Chromebook 3 includes a Celeron N4020, a relatively modern dual-core chip, and Google support that only expires in 2026.</p>



<p>We&rsquo;re going to warn you: there are other sites offering Chromebooks for this $79 price or less, especially Walmart. Beware of refurbished or &ldquo;recertified&rdquo; Chromebooks, and watch out for Chromebooks offering an N2840 or a Celeron N3000-esque processor inside. These were made several years ago, and just aren&rsquo;t worth the savings. </p>



<p>If your Chromebook budget is $100, we&rsquo;d ask that you try and squeeze an extra $20 out of it and opt for the <a href="https://shop-links.co/link/?url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.bestbuy.com%2Fsite%2Fasus-14-chromebook-intel-core-m3-8100y-4gb-memory-64gb-emmc-silver%2F6513085.p%3F&amp;publisher_slug=pcworld&amp;exclusive=1&amp;article_name=pcworld&amp;article_url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.pcworld.com%2Ffeed" rel="nofollow">$119 Asus 14-inch Chromebook</a> instead, on a massive 64% off sale at Best Buy. You&rsquo;ll get a <em>much</em> larger, better screen, and an improved processor. But if you can&rsquo;t, please choose the $79 Lenovo Chromebook 3 instead. It&rsquo;s easily the best sub-$100 Chromebook you&rsquo;ll find on Black Friday.</p>

## You can build a $500 gaming PC with these Black Friday deals
 - [https://www.pcworld.com/article/1394611/you-can-build-a-500-gaming-pc-with-black-friday-deals-heres-how.html](https://www.pcworld.com/article/1394611/you-can-build-a-500-gaming-pc-with-black-friday-deals-heres-how.html)

 - date published: 2022-11-25 17:18:18+00:00
 - Starred: False

<div id="link_wrapped_content">
<section class="wp-block-bigbite-multi-title"><div class="container"></div></section><p>Putting together a $500 gaming PC usually requires sacrifices. A creaky older graphics card is the big one, and often less memory and less storage, too. But not during Black Friday.&nbsp;</p>



<p>Building at this time of year is <em>great</em>. You can stack the deals to get nice parts at big discounts. The results put prebuilt desktops <a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://www.newegg.com/p/3D5-000Z-000S1?Item=9SIA08CJJ14070&amp;xcust=2-2-1394611-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow">in the same price range</a> to shame. Right now you can roll a system capable of 1080p Ultra at 60fps, with an easy path for future upgrades, for $500 or less. All the parts are new and are sold by first-party sellers only.</p>



<p>Have different needs? You can also move up to $700 for a 1440p build or scale down to under $400 for 720p, too. Just check out the example builds below.</p>

<p>As typical for suggested gaming PC builds, the cost of a mouse and keyboard aren&rsquo;t included in the list. You can request a free loaner boot kit from AMD for this purpose. A local computer shop may also be able to perform this service for a fee.</em></li><li><em>Price is after </em><a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://images10.newegg.com/uploadfilesfornewegg/rebate/SH/MSI33%20MIRsNov1Nov3022nm13us.pdf&amp;xcust=2-2-1394611-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow"><em>$20 mail-in rebate</em></a><em>. MIR must be filed within 21 days of purchase.</em></li><li><em>Promotion valid with purchase of </em><a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://www.amd.com/en/gaming/ryzen-uncharted-bundle&amp;xcust=2-2-1394611-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow"><em>a qualifying AMD CPU</em></a><em> from AMD, Amazon, Micro Center, or Newegg.</em></li><li><em>Promotion valid with purchase of </em><a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://www.amd.com/en/gaming/raise-the-game&amp;xcust=2-2-1394611-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow"><em>a qualifying AMD graphics card</em></a><em> from AMD, Amazon, Micro Center, or Newegg.</em></li></ol><p>This system nets you a build with a solid 6-core, 12-thread processor, a micro-ATX Wi-Fi motherboard that supports RGB and ARGB fans, 16GB of DDR4-3600 memory (Ryzen 3000 and 5000&rsquo;s sweet spot for RAM speed), our top recommendation for NVMe Gen 3 SSDs, a power supply rated as Tier B <a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://cultists.network/140/psu-tier-list/&amp;xcust=2-2-1394611-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow">on this respected list</a>, and a solid airflow case. And yes, the Windows 10 license is included&mdash;no cheating here. (Full disclosure: I was tempted to.) The key comes from PCWorld&rsquo;s affiliated software store, so it&rsquo;s above board.</p>



<p>Oh, and again, this build also includes three bonus games (technically four). This is <em>a lot</em> for a build between $500 and $600. Remember the prebuilt mentioned above? That has a weaker lower core count processor, much weaker graphics card, half the memory (and slower memory at that), and no free software. This build smokes it, even without any RGB fans.</p>



<p>The main caveats? You need to flash the motherboard&rsquo;s BIOS to a newer version before the Ryzen 5 5500 will work in it. You can request a <a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://www.amd.com/en/support/kb/faq/pa-105&amp;xcust=2-2-1394611-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow">free loaner boot kit from AMD</a> for this purpose. A local computer shop may also be able to perform this service for a fee. (Or a good friend for free, if they like you.) This build also only supports PCIe 3.0, but SSDs and graphics card running at that standard&rsquo;s speeds will still be plenty fast for a long while.</p>



<h4 id="areas-for-improvement">Areas for improvement</h4>



<ul><li><strong>Storage:</strong> A 500GB SSD will fill up pretty quick, especially if you play big blockbuster AAA games. If you can afford it, buy the <a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://www.amazon.com/dp/B0B25LZGGW/ref=twister_B0B5FJCDGT?_encoding=UTF8&amp;psc=1&amp;xcust=2-2-1394611-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow">1TB version of the Crucial P3</a> ($63) instead.</li><li><strong>Additional fans / alternative case:</strong> My original pick, <a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://www.newegg.com/p/11-353-185?item=11-353-185&amp;xcust=2-2-1394611-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow">this $53 DIYPC case</a>, included several RGB fans but sold out by Black Friday proper. (This is why you should start monitoring deals at the end of October.) Its substitute only has one included fan. You can buy more fans yourself for optimal airflow, which will give you control over performance, or you can pay about $10 more for the <a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://www.newegg.com/p/2AM-000R-001B6?Item=9SIAGRZBZU2540&amp;xcust=2-2-1394611-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow">Bitfenix Nova Mesh</a>, which comes outfitted with four RGB fans.</li></ul><h4 id="suggested-upgrades">Suggested upgrades:</h4>



<ul><li><strong>Memory:</strong> 16GB will hold work for many people who primarily game and don&rsquo;t have a lot of things open at the same time. But if you&rsquo;re a browser tab hoarder (hi), stepping up to <a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://www.amazon.com/dp/B08MDZ9YFR&amp;xcust=2-2-1394611-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow">32GB of RAM</a> ($80) isn&rsquo;t much more expensive right now.&nbsp;</li><li><strong>Motherboard:</strong> An ATX motherboard will support more expansion cards, like an internal game capture card and/or a sound card. Newegg has these <a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://www.newegg.com/gigabyte-b450-aorus-elite-v2/p/N82E16813145251?Item=N82E16813145251&amp;xcust=2-2-1394611-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow">$100 Gigabyte B450 Aorus Elite</a>, <a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://www.newegg.com/asrock-b450-steel-legend/p/N82E16813157869?Item=N82E16813157869&amp;xcust=2-2-1394611-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow">$105 ASRock B450 Steel Legend</a>, and <a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://www.newegg.com/gigabyte-b450-aorus-pro-wifi/p/N82E16813145082?Item=N82E16813145082&amp;xcust=2-2-1394611-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow">$120 Gigabyte B450 Aorus Pro Wi-Fi</a> models that are worth a look.</li><li><strong>Storage:</strong> Whether you stick with the suggested 500GB SSD or move up to a 1TB model as your boot drive, it doesn&rsquo;t hurt to still have more storage available. This $47 <a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://www.amazon.com/Seagate-BarraCuda-Internal-Drive-3-5-Inch/dp/B07H2RR55Q&amp;xcust=2-2-1394611-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow">2TB Seagate Barracuda HDD</a> runs at 7,200RPM, making it a faster option. (For a spinning platter drive, anyway.)</li></ul><h3 id="alternatives">Alternatives</h3>



<h5 id="micro-center-variant-483">Micro Center variant &ndash; $483</h5>



<ul><li>Swap in this <a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://www.microcenter.com/product/5006114/amd-ryzen-5-3600-with-wraith-stealth-cooler,-gigabyte-b450m-ds3h-wifi,-cpu-motherboard-combo?storeid=101&amp;xcust=2-2-1394611-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow">$130 Ryzen 5 3600 CPU + Gigabyte B450M Wi-FI motherboard combo</a> (available in-store only), opt instead for this <a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://www.microcenter.com/product/643497/montech-x1-tempered-glass-atx-mid-tower-computer-case-black&amp;xcust=2-2-1394611-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow">$50 Montech X1 case</a>, and ditch the Windows 10 license for Linux, and you&rsquo;ve got yourself a very nice sub-$500 gaming PC.&nbsp;<br /><br />Even if you keep Windows, you&rsquo;ll still sit at $533 total, which is cheaper overall. That said&mdash;if you&rsquo;re extremely lucky, your Micro Center may have <a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://www.microcenter.com/product/651303/inland-qn322-2tb-ssd-nvme-pcie-gen-30-x4-m2-2280-3d-nand-qlc-internal-solid-state-drive&amp;xcust=2-2-1394611-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow">this $80 2TB NVMe Gen 3 M.2 SSD</a> in stock. Scraping Windows would pay for putting into your build instead of the Crucial P3 and quadrupling your space. Speeds are better on the P3, though.</li></ul><h5 id="bare-bones-variant-508">Bare-bones variant &ndash; $508</h5>



<ul><li>If you must slash costs, you <em>could</em> switch to this <a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://www.newegg.com/asrock-b450m-pro4-r2-0/p/N82E16813157973?Item=N82E16813157973&amp;xcust=2-2-1394611-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow">$70 motherboard without Wi-Fi</a>, drop to <a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://www.corsair.com/us/en/Categories/Products/Memory/VENGEANCE-LPX/p/CMK8GX4M1Z3600C18&amp;xcust=2-2-1394611-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow">8GB of memory</a>, and install Linux instead for $70 in savings. Don&rsquo;t nerf the RAM that hard, though. Saving that $10 isn&rsquo;t worth it.</li></ul><h2 class="toc" id="the-700-1440p-black-friday-gaming-pc-build">The $700 1440p Black Friday gaming PC build</h2>

<ol><li><em>This motherboard requires flashing to a newer BIOS before it will work with Ryzen 5000 processors. You can request a free loaner boot kit from AMD for this purpose. A local computer shop may also be able to perform this service for a fee.</em></li><li><em>Promotion valid with purchase of </em><a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://www.amd.com/en/gaming/ryzen-uncharted-bundle&amp;xcust=2-2-1394611-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow"><em>a qualifying AMD CPU</em></a><em> from AMD, Amazon, Micro Center, or Newegg.</em></li><li><em>Promotion valid with purchase of </em><a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://www.amd.com/en/gaming/raise-the-game&amp;xcust=2-2-1394611-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow"><em>a qualifying AMD graphics card</em></a><em> from AMD, Amazon, Micro Center, or Newegg.</em></li></ol><p>This 1440p build sports a 6-core, 12-thread processor that supports PCIe 4.0, an ATX board capable of powering RGB and ARGB fans, 16GB of DDR4-3600 memory (Ryzen 3000 and 5000&rsquo;s sweet spot for RAM speed), our top recommendation for NVMe Gen 3 SSDs, and a solid airflow case. A Windows 10 license is included, too, and comes from PCWorld&rsquo;s affiliated software store. Plus, it qualifies for three bonus games. Thank you, AMD.</p>



<p>At this price point, trimming corners with a cheaper CPU just doesn&rsquo;t make sense. Better to invest a little bit more money to future-proof with PCIe 4.0 support. And cutting down on memory and storage capacity feels stingy.</p>



<p>The only caveat here is the power supply&mdash;if you have the money, upgrade to something with more longevity and a higher wattage, like this <a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://www.newegg.com/thermaltake-toughpower-gf1-tt-premium-edition-ps-tpd-0850fnfaga-1-850w/p/N82E16817153403?Item=N82E16817153403&amp;xcust=2-2-1394611-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow">$80 Thermaltake GF1 80+ Gold</a> model. It&rsquo;ll survive this build (likely another one after, too) and support a beefier graphics card later on, if you so choose. Also, you&rsquo;ll need to flash the BIOS before the Ryzen 5 5600 will work in the motherboard.</p>



<h4 id="suggested-upgrades">Suggested upgrades:</h4>



<ul><li><strong>Memory:</strong> Never met a browser tab you didn&rsquo;t leave open? Stepping up to <a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://www.amazon.com/dp/B08MDZ9YFR&amp;xcust=2-2-1394611-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow">32GB of RAM</a> ($80) doesn&rsquo;t cost much more.</li><li><strong>Storage:</strong> <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/1384710/">2TB SSDs don&rsquo;t cost too much more right now</a>, and if you want go to for blistering speed, PCIe Gen 4 models have hit all-time lows.</li></ul><h2 class="toc" id="the-390-fortnite-black-friday-gaming-pc-build">The $390 Fortnite Black Friday gaming PC build</h2>

<p>But as configured, it&rsquo;s somewhat limited. The power supply will restrict you to budget graphics cards, should you want to upgrade to a discrete GPU in the future. <div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-block faq-block"><h2 class="faq-block-title" id="faq"> FAQ </h2><hr class="block-horizotal-divider" /><div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-inner-block faq-save-block"><div class="faq-save-content"><span class="faq-rank">1.</span>
<h3 id="are-black-friday-monitor-deals-really-worth-it">Are Black Friday monitor deals really worth it?</h3>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-answer-block how-to-tip">
<p>Yes, absolutely, you can find some great deals on monitors during the week of Black Friday&mdash;as evidenced by the great deals in the article above. Mind you, in some tech categories&mdash;like say, wireless earbuds or phone chargers&mdash;you&rsquo;ll see discounts on off-brand gear we&rsquo;d never recommend. But when it comes to monitors, highly reputable brands like HP, Dell, Samsung and Lenovo will drop prices on great models. PCWorld strives to only recommend deals on solid monitors that are experiencing legitimate pricing drops. To this end, we look for models that have reached or fallen below their all-time-low prices.</p>
</div>
</div></div>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-inner-block faq-save-block"><div class="faq-save-content"><span class="faq-rank">2.</span>
<h3 id="are-black-friday-monitor-deals-lower-quality">Are Black Friday monitor deals lower quality?</h3>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-answer-block how-to-tip">
<p>No, there&rsquo;s no reason why the monitor deals you find during Black Friday should be lower quality&mdash;at least if you focus on the big-name manufacturers like Samsung, Philips, LG, Dell, HP, Lenovo and so on. It&rsquo;s true that some of the discounted monitors may be 2021 models, but there&rsquo;s nothing wrong with that. Monitor tech moves rather slowly and there won&rsquo;t be major quality differences between 2021 and 2022 models. The important thing is to get a monitor at a legitimately lower price&mdash;and we have done the heavy lifting to curate those legit deals.</p>
</div>
</div></div>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-inner-block faq-save-block"><div class="faq-save-content"><span class="faq-rank">3.</span>
<h3 id="what-should-i-look-for-in-a-black-friday-monitor">What should I look for in a Black Friday monitor?</h3>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-answer-block how-to-tip">
<p>Ah, we&rsquo;ve arrived at the question of the hour.</p>



<p>Let&rsquo;s first talk about refresh rate, which is important if you&rsquo;re looking for a gaming monitor. The refresh rate is how fast a monitor can redraw the image on its screen. The faster the refresh rate, the smoother your visuals will look. For competitive first-person shooters, we&rsquo;d recommend 120Hz as the minimum rate. Anything higher is good enough for the eSports realm.</p>



<p>Resolution is another important feature to consider. Much like the refresh rate, the higher the number, the better. We&rsquo;re talking about the quality of images and video here. 1080p is the bare minimum for most&nbsp;monitors. However, if you&rsquo;re a video editor, bumping the resolution up to 4K makes a massive difference, as it allows you to see more detail.</p>



<p>The final thing is the screen size. 27 inches is the most common and a good size for a home office. For gaming monitors, 24 or 27 inches is best. Sometimes a larger screen causes eye strain and if you&rsquo;re going to be staring at one for hours, it&rsquo;s better to go a bit smaller. For 4K monitors, 32-inches is a good option, as it gives you quite a bit of screen to work with.</p>
</div>
</div></div>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-inner-block faq-save-block"><div class="faq-save-content"><span class="faq-rank">4.</span>
<h3 id="where-can-i-find-the-highest-rated-monitors">Where can I find the highest rated monitors?</h3>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-answer-block how-to-tip">
<p>PCWorld&nbsp;reviews&nbsp;new monitors every month. So, if you want to see the models we&rsquo;ve rated the highest, check out our rankings for the&nbsp;<a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/811315/best-monitors-2.html">best monitors of 2022</a>. We also have more granular picks on the&nbsp;<a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/813301/best-gaming-monitors.html">best gaming monitors</a>, as well as the&nbsp;<a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/813361/best-4k-monitors.html">best 4K monitors for desktop workstations</a>. Come Black Friday, a lot of our top picks may be on sale, so don&rsquo;t limit your shopping only to the deals we&rsquo;ve called out above.</p>
</div>
</div></div>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-inner-block faq-save-block"><div class="faq-save-content"><span class="faq-rank">5.</span>
<h3 id="what-black-friday-retailers-should-i-check-out">What Black Friday retailers should I check out?</h3>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-answer-block how-to-tip">
<p>Amazon&rsquo;s going to have a slew of awesome deals. That&rsquo;s a given. However, for monitors, you should definitely peruse the main pages of HP, Dell and Lenovo. Personally, I find myself going directly to the manufacturers more often than not. You can also widen your net and scope out other online retailers like Best Buy and Newegg.</p>
</div>
</div></div>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-inner-block faq-save-block"><div class="faq-save-content"><span class="faq-rank">6.</span>
<h3 id="when-is-black-friday-2022">When is Black Friday 2022?</h3>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-answer-block how-to-tip">
<p>Black Friday is on Friday, Nov 25th 2022. If you consider yourself an avid deals hunter, we&rsquo;d suggest going online in the early hours to take advantage of the best deals. Deals tend to change and expire at a breakneck pace.</p>
</div>
</div></div>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-inner-block faq-save-block"><div class="faq-save-content"><span class="faq-rank">7.</span>
<h3 id="when-is-cyber-monday-2022">When is Cyber Monday 2022?</h3>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-answer-block how-to-tip">
<p>Cyber Monday is on Monday, Nov 28th 2022. For the best deals, we&rsquo;d recommend logging on at midnight, as stock tends to deplete rather quickly.</p>

## How to check your laptopâ€™s battery health
 - [https://www.pcworld.com/article/394918/how-to-check-your-laptops-battery-health.html](https://www.pcworld.com/article/394918/how-to-check-your-laptops-battery-health.html)
 - RSS feed: https://www.pcworld.com/index.rss
 - date published: 2022-11-25 11:45:00+00:00
 - Starred: False

<div id="link_wrapped_content">
<section class="wp-block-bigbite-multi-title"><div class="container"></div></section><p>Battery life is an often vague and nebulous concept. In theory, it can be represented by a single number but, in practice, literally hundreds of factors can shorten or lengthen endurance. That&rsquo;s frustrating if you&rsquo;re trying to gauge the battery life and health of your notebook, especially if you&rsquo;re trying to determine if it&rsquo;s time to <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/2854456/the-best-pc-laptops-of-the-year.html">buy a new laptop</a>.</p>



<p>Windows has a secret feature called Battery Report that can help. It&rsquo;s what we use while testing notebook endurance at PCWorld&mdash;and it&rsquo;s how you can tell if <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/1377160/your-laptops-battery-life-may-be-dropping-faster-than-you-think.html">your laptop&rsquo;s battery life is dropping faster than you think</a>. Here&rsquo;s how to access Battery Report and understand what it reveals you about your laptop.</p>



<h2 id="how-to-create-a-battery-report">How to create a Battery Report</h2>



<p>Battery Report is not a new feature, but it remains under-the-radar because there&rsquo;s no way to access it through Windows&rsquo; settings menus. You can only create a Battery Report through the Command Prompt. Here&rsquo;s how to do it:</p>



<ul><li>Perform a Windows Search for <strong>CMD </strong>or <strong>Command Prompt</strong>. You&rsquo;ll see Command Prompt appear and the search results. Open it. Alternatively, you can find Command Prompt listed under Windows System in the Windows Start menu.</li><li>Once open, you&rsquo;ll see a command line starting with C: and ending with the name of your user account. A blinking cursor will appear at the end of this command line. Type <strong>powercfg /batteryreport</strong> and press <strong>Enter</strong> on your keyboard.</li><li>If successful, the Command Prompt will tell you a battery life report was saved to your user folder.</li><li>Navigate to the folder listed in the Command Prompt. This will be your default user folder, which is C:Users&lt;yourusername&gt;</li></ul><div class="extendedBlock-wrapper block-coreImage undefined"><figure class="wp-block-image"><a class="zoom" href="https://images.idgesg.net/images/article/2021/07/command-prompt-100896507-orig.jpg" rel="nofollow"><img alt="command prompt" src="https://images.idgesg.net/images/article/2021/07/command-prompt-100896507-large.jpg?auto=webp&amp;quality=85,70" /></a><figcaption><p>The Windows Command Prompt.</p>
</figcaption></figure></div>




<p>You can access the Battery Report either by using File Explorer to navigate to your user folder, or by performing a Windows Search for <strong>battery report</strong>. Note that it may take several minutes for Windows Search to index the new report and allow you to search for it, so File Explorer might be faster.&nbsp;</p>



<p>The Battery Report is saved as an HTML document, so you can open it with the web browser of your choice. Once open you&rsquo;ll find a long document that is packed with information. Here&rsquo;s how to decipher what each section means.</p>



<h2 id="how-to-use-battery-report-to-estimate-battery-life">How to use Battery Report to estimate battery life</h2>



<p>The Battery Report can be used to gauge battery life in a few ways, but most people will want to scroll to the bottom of the report where you&rsquo;ll find the <strong>Battery life estimates </strong>section.<strong>&nbsp; </strong></p>



<p>This does the math calculating how long the battery could last based on how long you&rsquo;ve used it each day or week. The estimate is handy because you don&rsquo;t have to fully drain the battery.</p>



<p>Take a look at the Active column under At Full Charge. This will show a result formatted in hours, minutes, and seconds. If the column says 4:56:22, for instance, that means the battery was estimated to last four hours, 56 minutes, and 22 seconds.</p>


<div class="extendedBlock-wrapper block-coreImage undefined"><figure class="wp-block-image"><a class="zoom" href="https://images.idgesg.net/images/article/2021/07/battery-life-estimates-100896510-orig.jpg" rel="nofollow"><img alt="battery life estimates" src="https://images.idgesg.net/images/article/2021/07/battery-life-estimates-100896510-large.jpg?auto=webp&amp;quality=85,70" /></a></figure></div>




<p>You will also notice the log lists At Full Charge and At Design Capacity. The At Full Charge column is the estimate you want to pay attention to, as it creates an estimate based on the maximum charge your laptop&rsquo;s battery can handle right now.</p>



<p>The At Design Capacity column creates an estimate based on the maximum battery charge of your laptop when it was new. This is a useful comparison for an older laptop.</p>



<p>The log is not perfect. The estimate is based on how you used the battery in the past so it will be off if you change how you use the PC in the future. Even a minor change, like switching the web browser you use, can throw off the estimate.</p>



<p>Battery report&rsquo;s math can also prove a bit&hellip;odd, at times. You will see errors when a system is used for only a short period of time or in short bursts throughout the day. You may also notice errors if the system is not used at all for several weeks.</p>



<h2 id="how-to-use-battery-report-to-measure-battery-life">How to use Battery Report to measure battery life</h2>



<p>The battery life estimate is useful for a quick glance, but you&rsquo;ll need to go deeper if you want an accurate result.</p>



<p>Take a look at the Battery usage section of the report. This shows you how the battery was actually used in the last three days. You can try to piece together battery life using these snippets, but it&rsquo;s tough.</p>



<p>You can only record an accurate result by forcing your laptop to discharge its entire battery in one go. It&rsquo;s possible to do this while using the laptop normally, but it&rsquo;s easier to use a video, script, or benchmark that can run unattended. Here&rsquo;s a few suggestions:</p>



<ul><li>A YouTube video that&rsquo;s 10 hours long, or longer.</li><li>Use the <a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://web.basemark.com&amp;xcust=2-1-394918-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow">Basemark Web 3.0 benchmark</a>. Check the benchmark&rsquo;s configuration options and turn on Battery Life mode, which infinitely loops the benchmark.</li><li>Use <a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://chrome.google.com/webstore/detail/imacros-for-chrome/cplklnmnlbnpmjogncfgfijoopmnlemp?hl=en&amp;xcust=2-1-394918-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow">iMacros</a> to create a custom web browsing macro and then use the loop feature to run the macro until the battery is drained.</li><li>Use a program like <a href="https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=111346X1569483&amp;url=https://www.macrorecorder.com&amp;xcust=2-1-394918-1-0-0&amp;sref=https://www.pcworld.com/feed" rel="nofollow">Macro Recorder </a>to create a loop that repeats infinitely.</li></ul><p>Also turn off all sleep and hibernation features, including those that turn off or dim the display.</p>


<div class="extendedBlock-wrapper block-coreImage undefined"><figure class="wp-block-image"><a class="zoom" href="https://images.idgesg.net/images/article/2021/07/battery-usage-100896508-orig.jpg" rel="nofollow"><img alt="battery usage" src="https://images.idgesg.net/images/article/2021/07/battery-usage-100896508-large.jpg?auto=webp&amp;quality=85,70" /></a></figure></div>




<p>Start your chosen test and wait until the laptop reaches its critical battery state. It will automatically power off. Connect the laptop to power, turn it on, and run the battery report again. The Battery usage section of the report will tell you how long the battery endured.</p>



<p>Running this test will give you an accurate endurance baseline. You can compare it to similar tests from other people who own the same system, or you can run the test every month to see how battery life holds up over time.</p>



<h2 id="how-to-use-battery-report-to-measure-battery-health">How to use Battery Report to measure battery health</h2>



<p>Battery Report offers two more ways to decide if your battery is over the hill.</p>



<p>The first is Cycle Count, which you&rsquo;ll find near the top of the report under <strong>Installed Batteries</strong>. Cycle count is an estimate of how many times your laptop&rsquo;s full battery capacity has been discharged.</p>



<p>This is cumulative: one cycle can mean the battery was discharged by 20 percent five times, or 100 percent once. A typical laptop battery should handle several hundred charge cycles before there&rsquo;s any meaningful change in battery capacity. Most can handle 500 to 1,000 cycles before battery capacity becomes a problem.</p>



<p>You can also examine the <strong>Battery capacity history</strong> section found halfway through the report. This provides a log of measured battery capacity and also, for convenience, shows the battery&rsquo;s design capacity, which is how much power the battery should hold if it performed as intended.</p>


<div class="extendedBlock-wrapper block-coreImage undefined"><figure class="wp-block-image"><a class="zoom" href="https://images.idgesg.net/images/article/2021/07/battery-capacity-history-100896509-orig.jpg" rel="nofollow"><img alt="battery capacity history" src="https://images.idgesg.net/images/article/2021/07/battery-capacity-history-100896509-large.jpg?auto=webp&amp;quality=85,70" /></a></figure></div>




<p>Many new laptops will show a full charge capacity that&rsquo;s a bit higher than the design capacity, but the <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/1377160/your-laptops-battery-life-may-be-dropping-faster-than-you-think.html">full charge capacity will decrease as the battery ages</a>. The laptop above, for instance, is approaching its tenth birthday.</p>



<p>A full charge capacity that&rsquo;s 20 percent lower than the original design capacity, or lower, indicates an older battery. There&rsquo;s nothing to stop you from running a battery into the ground, though. A modern laptop battery will stop working entirely long before its full charge capacity reaches zero.</p>
Laptops</div>

## Monitor buying guide: How to choose your next display
 - [https://www.pcworld.com/article/535837/monitor_buying_guide.html](https://www.pcworld.com/article/535837/monitor_buying_guide.html)
 - RSS feed: https://www.pcworld.com/index.rss
 - date published: 2022-11-25 11:30:00+00:00
 - Starred: False

<div id="link_wrapped_content">
<section class="wp-block-bigbite-multi-title"><div class="container"></div></section><p>First, the good news: Most modern PC monitors are rather decent. Their minimum brightness, contrast, and color accuracy have improved significantly over the past decade. It&rsquo;s a great time to upgrade even if you stick to budget monitors.</p>



<p>If you want a quick, easy recommendation: Go for a 24-inch monitor with 1080p resolution or a 27-inch monitor with 1440p resolution. An IPS panel is preferable, though VA is also good. Gamers can spend a little more to snag either option with a 144Hz refresh rate, which offers a smoother and more responsive experience. For more concrete recommendations, be sure to check out our roundups of <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/811315/best-monitors-2.html">the best monitors</a> overall, the <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/813301/best-gaming-monitors.html">best gaming monitors</a>, and the <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/813361/best-4k-monitors.html">best 4K monitors</a>. We also have more specialized guides to the <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/1377172/best-usb-c-monitors.html">best USB-C monitors</a>, the <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/1382692/best-monitors-for-graphics-design.html">best monitors for graphic design</a>, and the <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/1381002/best-monitors-for-programming.html">best monitors for programing</a>. Our picks are the result of hundreds of hours spent testing the latest monitors from Acer, Asus, BenQ, Dell, LG, Samsung, and other major brands.</p>



<p>Not sure that&rsquo;s right for you, or want to know more about the tech? Here&rsquo;s the lay of the land.</p>



<h2 id="monitor-types-tn-ips-va-and-oled-panels">Monitor types: TN, IPS, VA, and OLED panels</h2>



		<div class="wp-block-product-widget-block product-widget">
			<div class="product-widget__block-title-wrapper">
				<h4 class="product-widget__block-title" id="an-eco-friendly-monitor-on-a-budget">

			</div>

<p>The technology behind monitors is complex but well understood. There&rsquo;s just a handful of major &ldquo;monitor types&rdquo; available, each defined by the LCD panel technology used. Nearly all monitors available today fall into these groups.</p>



<p>Monitor manufacturers will list panel type in a monitor&rsquo;s specifications, but you may have to dig a bit to find it. Take the extra time to find out. Panel type can tell you a lot about a monitor.</p>



<h3 id="in-plane-switching-ips">In-Plane Switching (IPS)</h3>



<p>IPS rules the world of computer monitors. A typical IPS monitor is bright and crisp, with good sharpness and great viewing angles. Color performance ranges from acceptable to truly spectacular. Modern IPS monitors can support fast pixel response times and high refresh rates, which is good news for gamers.</p>



<p>IPS monitors have disappointing contrast and black levels, however, which can make them appear hazy when viewing dark images. This is most noticeable in a dark room.</p>



<h3 id="vertical-alignment-va">Vertical Alignment (VA)</h3>



<p>Increasingly popular, VA monitors are as bright and colorful as their IPS counterparts and have a better contrast ratio and darker black levels, which improves overall image quality. VA monitors designed for gaming can offer excellent motion clarity, and Samsung&rsquo;s best VA panel monitors are particularly crisp.</p>



<p>Viewing angles are more limited, however, so the VA monitor image quality can degrade if not viewed straight-on. IPS monitors also have better motion clarity at most price points.</p>



		<div class="wp-block-product-widget-block product-widget">
			<div class="product-widget__block-title-wrapper">
				<h4 class="product-widget__block-title" id="the-best-budget-monitor-for-graphic-design">
					the best budget monitor for graphic design				</h4>
			</div>

			<div class="product-widget__content-wrapper">
									<div class="product-widget__title-wrapper">
						<h3 class="product-widget__title" id="nzxt-canvas-27q">NZXT Canvas 27Q</h3>
					</div>

					</div>

						</div>
									</div>
			</div>
		</div>

		


<h3 id="twisted-nematic-tn-technology">Twisted Nematic (TN) technology</h3>



<p>TN panels are known for being inexpensive to make. They also have very quick pixel response times, which improves motion clarity.</p>



<p>Unfortunately, TN has limitations in contrast and color performance that make it unattractive, so I can only recommend TN to extremely hardcore gamers. BenQ&rsquo;s Zowie line is a good choice for those on the &ldquo;path to pro.&rdquo;</p>



<h3 id="organic-light-emitting-diode-oled">Organic Light Emitting Diode (OLED)</h3>



<p>OLED isn&rsquo;t based on LCD technology at all. It instead uses organic pixel elements that emit their own light (a trait often referred to as &ldquo;self emissive&rdquo;). OLED is the king of contrast and black levels, since an OLED pixel that&rsquo;s turned off emits no light at all. OLED generally beats other panel types in color performance and also has best-in-class motion clarity. Viewing angles are great, too.</p>



<p>OLED panels aren&rsquo;t as bright as the competition at the top end, and OLED can suffer permanent image retention over time (though this takes many thousands of hours). The technology is also very expensive in PC monitors.</p>



<h3 id="sowhats-the-best-monitor-type">So&hellip;what&rsquo;s the best monitor type?</h3>



<p>OLED wins out on image quality, but high pricing and limited availability mean I can&rsquo;t recommend it for everyone. It&rsquo;s too expensive and too hard to find.</p>



<p>That leaves IPS with the crown for most people, though a VA panel monitor could be a better choice if you don&rsquo;t view from an angle and want improved image quality in movies and TV shows.</p>



<h3 id="a-note-about-mini-led">A note about Mini-LED</h3>


<div class="extendedBlock-wrapper block-coreImage undefined"><figure class="wp-block-image size-large"><img alt="Samsung Odyssey Neo G9 mini-LED monitor" class="wp-image-560234" height="800" src="https://b2c-contenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/12/samsung-odyssey-neo-g9.jpg?quality=50&amp;strip=all&amp;w=1200" width="1200" /></figure><p class="imageCredit">Matt Smith/IDG</p></div>



<p>A handful of monitors are now available with <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/560224/oled-vs-mini-led-the-pc-displays-of-the-future-compared.html">Mini-LED technology</a>. This is a backlight technology, not a panel technology, but still important.</p>



<p>Mini-LED uses an array of independent LED lighting zones behind the display panel to precisely control the backlight. In my testing, a Mini-LED monitor can offer a 300 to 600 percent improvement in contrast when compared to similar monitors that lack Mini-LED. It&rsquo;s extremely noticeable.</p>



<p>You&rsquo;ll find Mini-LED available with both IPS and VA monitor types. The traits of each panel type still otherwise apply. OLED is not used with Mini-LED because the panel creates its own light, making a backlight unnecessary.</p>



<p>Mini-LED has a few flaws. The backlight zones can cause bright halos to appear around objects, an issue known as blooming. It&rsquo;s most noticeable in a dark room. It&rsquo;s also expensive to make, so you&rsquo;ll only find Mini-LED in premium monitors.</p>



<p>The number of Mini-LED lighting zones matters. A basic Mini-LED monitor like <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/797584/sonys-stylish-ps5-monitors-and-headsets-play-nice-with-gaming-pcs.html">the Sony InZone</a> offers 96, while the extravagant and <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/394490/ive-fallen-in-love-with-this-asus-miniled-4k-panel.html">awesome Asus ROG Swift PG32UQX </a>has 1,152. More zones means better overall contrast and less blooming.</p>



<h2 id="monitor-size-pick-what-feels-comfortable-to-you">Monitor size: Pick what feels comfortable to you</h2>

<p>Most monitors consist of a 24-inch, 27-inch, or 32-inch widescreen panel. It&rsquo;s easy to assume bigger is better, but it&rsquo;s also important how a display fits within a person&rsquo;s field of view. This means all parts of the display are visible without eye strain or head movement.</p>



<p>Still, monitor size is very much a matter of personal preference. I tend to like smaller displays that don&rsquo;t take up too much desk space and can be used easily in a <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/448298/how-to-set-up-two-monitors.html">multi-monitor setup</a>. Others may like <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/395110/ultrawide-vs-dual-monitors.html">one big display</a> that takes up the entire desk.</p>



<h2 id="monitor-resolution-1080p-is-common-but-4k-is-obtainable">Monitor resolution: 1080p is common, but 4K is obtainable</h2>



<p>Most budget monitors have a native resolution of 1080p (1920&times;1080). This is okay for 24-inch monitors, but the lack of sharpness becomes obvious on larger displays.</p>



<p>27-inch and 32-inch models are better at 1440p (2560&times;1440) resolution. Most people will notice the increase in sharpness even when browsing the web. It&rsquo;s a great resolution for gaming as well, though PlayStation fans be warned: the PS4 and PS5 don&rsquo;t support this resolution.</p>



<p>4K (3840&times;2160) is ideal for larger monitors. It&rsquo;s also a great upgrade for 27-inch and 32-inch monitors. The added sharpness isn&rsquo;t a must-have, but it&rsquo;s noticeable, especially if you like to use a small font size on your monitor. Games and 4K movies will look razor-sharp.</p>



<p>Pricing is a consideration. Lower resolutions mean lower pricing, which is why 1080p remains so popular. The gap has narrowed in recent years, however, with 4K monitors now starting just below $300.</p>

<p>Ultrawide monitors, which have a 21:9 aspect ratio, are widely available. A 34-inch ultrawide is about as tall as a 27-inch widescreen but seven inches wider. This works out to a 25 percent larger display overall.</p>



<p>This is excellent for people who want more display space but don&rsquo;t want the hassle of a multi-monitor setup. Ultrawides are awesome for games and movies, too, providing an immersive experience. You&rsquo;ll pay more for an ultrawide, with quality models starting around $400.</p>



<p>Intrigued? <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/394848/are-ultrawide-monitors-worth-it.html">Our guide to ultrawide monitors</a> lists all the perks.</p>



<h2 id="monitor-refresh-rate-to-144hz-and-beyond">Monitor refresh rate: To 144Hz, and beyond!</h2>



		<div class="wp-block-product-widget-block product-widget">

<p>A monitor&rsquo;s refresh rate is the number of times it can update the display&rsquo;s image each second. Most monitors have a 60Hz refresh rate, but some have a 144Hz, 240Hz, or 360Hz refresh rate, <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/704823/the-new-asus-500hz-gaming-monitor-is-the-worlds-fastest.html">with 500Hz models on the way</a>.</p>



<p>Higher refresh rates look smoother when images are in motion. It also lowers input lag because a new image appears on the display more frequently. The benefits improve as refresh rates go up, though the differences may become more difficult to notice.</p>



<p>Those who don&rsquo;t care about gaming can safely stick to 60Hz, while most gamers will appreciate the upgrade to 144Hz. Refresh rates beyond that are smoother but an optional luxury rather than a must-have.</p>



<h3><strong>A</strong>daptive sync: Common and useful</h3>



<p>Adaptive Sync can synchronize a PC&rsquo;s video output with the refresh rate of a display. This offers perfect frame pacing with no hitches, hesitations, or screen tearing (so long as the PC&rsquo;s hardware is up to the task at hand, at least). Adaptive Sync is a must-have feature for PC gamers, but it&rsquo;s common even on budget monitors meant for productivity and office work.</p>



<p>AMD FreeSync and Nvidia G-Sync are common standards. They&rsquo;re designed to work with each company&rsquo;s respective video cards, so it&rsquo;s important to pay attention to which standards a monitor supports. There&rsquo;s also a third-party standard called VESA AdaptiveSync. AMD, Intel, and Nvidia all support VESA AdaptiveSync in their latest graphics solutions, though functionality may be more limited than using the company&rsquo;s in-house standard.</p>



<p>Though mostly for gaming, Adaptive Sync is common and has no real price premium attached to it. It&rsquo;s an easy feature to recommend.</p>



<h2 id="monitor-ergonomics-adjustable-stands-rule">Monitor ergonomics: Adjustable stands rule</h2>



<p>Monitors ship with a variety of stands ranging from fixed plastic bases with no adjustment to complex monitor arms that can hold a monitor at almost any angle and orientation.</p>



<p>I recommend a stand that at least adjusts for height and tilt. This will let you find a comfortable viewing angle. If the monitor is a second display, look for swivel (which adjusts the angle horizontally) and pivot (which can rotate the monitor 90 degrees).&nbsp;</p>



<p>Look for monitors that have a 100x100mm VESA mount. This will let you add a third-party monitor stand or arm later. Most monitors sold today have this&mdash;but some budget models don&rsquo;t.</p>



<h2 id="monitor-hdr-its-usually-a-trap">Monitor HDR: It&rsquo;s (usually) a trap</h2>



		<div class="wp-block-product-widget-block product-widget">
			<div class="product-widget__block-title-wrapper">
				<h4 class="product-widget__block-title" id="a-big-brilliant-monitor-thats-held-back-by-hdr">
					A big, brilliant monitor that&rsquo;s held back by HDR				</h4>
			</div>

			<div class="product-widget__content-wrapper">
									<div class="product-widget__title-wrapper">
						<h3 class="product-widget__title" id="dell-g3223d">Dell G3223D</h3>
					</div>
				
									<div class="product-widget__image-outer-wrapper">
						<div class="product-widget__image-wrapper">
							<img alt="Dell G3223D" class="product-widget__image" height="1000" src="https://b2c-contenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/05/4be84696-d3c3-4928-8ac7-a8de8e205a17-1.jpg?quality=50&amp;strip=all" width="1549" /></div>
					</div>
				
									<div class="review product-widget__review-details">

							</div>
											</div>
				
				<div class="product-widget__information">
				
									</div>
			</div>
		</div>

		


<p>Many monitors advertise support for High Dynamic Range (HDR) content. HDR can support a wider range of luminance and color than what&rsquo;s now called SDR. Generally speaking, HDR content on a great HDR display can look far more vivid and lifelike.</p>



<p>The key is a &ldquo;great HDR display,&rdquo; and&hellip;most monitors aren&rsquo;t that. HDR support merely means a monitor can accept and display an HDR signal. It promises nothing about the quality of the experience which, in most cases, is not good.</p>



<p>If you do want great HDR, look for a monitor with OLED or Mini-LED technology. These can deliver the range of contrast and color performance needed to make HDR truly stand out. Both are expensive, putting quality HDR out of reach for most people.</p>



<p>Already have an HDR monitor, or plan to buy one? <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/394712/everything-you-need-to-know-about-hdr-on-your-pc.html">Our guide to HDR on Windows will help you get started</a>.</p>



<h2 id="monitor-features-speakers-are-nice-but-look-for-usb-c">Monitor features: Speakers are nice, but look for USB-C</h2>



		<div class="wp-block-product-widget-block product-widget">

<p>Most monitors don&rsquo;t offer many added features that stand out from competitors. Some have speakers. Many don&rsquo;t. A few models offer a remote control. Still, most monitors are similar.</p>



<p>USB-C is the one key exception. A monitor with USB-C can charge a connected device, such as a laptop, or be used to extend connectivity like a USB-C hub.<a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/612470/you-should-buy-a-usb-c-hub-monitor-heres-what-you-need-to-know.html"> I&rsquo;ve detailed the many perks of USB-C in another guide</a>.</p>



<h2 id="monitor-shopping-tips-pricing-matters">Monitor shopping tips: Pricing matters</h2>



<p>A monitor&rsquo;s price is by far the most important single factor when shopping for a monitor.</p>



<p>Perhaps this seems obvious, but it&rsquo;s more true of monitors than most consumer tech. Monitor pricing sees huge swings based on availability and sales events.</p>



<p>LG&rsquo;s 27GL850-B is a great example. The Amazon.com price of this monitor swung between a high of $496.99 and a low of $299.99 in just three months between April 1, 2022 and June 30, 2022.</p>



<p>This pattern plays out across the entire monitor market, so it&rsquo;s important to compare sales before buying. Shopping at one retailer could mean overpaying by hundreds.</p>

<p>I&rsquo;ve tried to keep this monitor buying guide direct and to the point, but I&rsquo;ll admit it can still be a lot to take in. Here&rsquo;s a summary of what most people should look for.</p>



<ul><li><strong>Monitor type</strong>: IPS is the market leader, though VA is also good. OLED is spectacular but expensive. Avoid TN.</li><li><strong>Monitor size</strong>: A 27-inch monitor is the go-to choice. Go bigger if you prefer.</li><li><strong>Monitor resolution</strong>: 1440p is recommended, 4K is a nice upgrade.</li><li><strong>Monitor refresh rate</strong>: 60Hz is fine for productivity, but 144Hz is awesome in games.</li><li><strong>Monitor adaptive sync</strong>: It&rsquo;s a must-have for gamers.</li><li><strong>Monitor stand</strong>: Look for height and tilt adjustment, plus VESA mount support.</li><li><strong>Monitor HDR: </strong>Only essential in Mini-LED and OLED monitors.</li><li><strong>Monitor features</strong>: Look for USB-C if you want to use the monitor as a USB-C hub.</li></ul><p>Ready to go even deeper? Once again, be sure to check out our roundups of <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/811315/best-monitors-2.html">the best monitors</a> overall, the <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/813301/best-gaming-monitors.html">best gaming monitors</a>, and the <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/813361/best-4k-monitors.html">best 4K monitors</a>. Our picks are the result of hundreds of hours spent testing the latest monitors from Acer, Asus, BenQ, Dell, LG, Samsung, and other major brands.</p>

<div id="link_wrapped_content">
<section class="wp-block-bigbite-multi-title"><div class="container"></div></section><p>Black Friday is here and ready to slay, which means a slew of monitor deals are popping up all over the place like an unhinged game of whack-a-mole. If you&rsquo;ve got no idea where to begin your search, don&rsquo;t worry. We put together a list of the best monitor deals available right now. From high refresh rate gaming monitors to super sharp 4K workstations, there&rsquo;s something for every type of buyer. If you&rsquo;re looking for other tech deals, we&rsquo;d recommend checking out <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/black-friday">PCWorld&rsquo;s complete Black Friday deals coverage</a>.</p>



<h2 id="best-black-friday-gaming-monitor-deals">Best Black Friday gaming monitor deals</h2>



<p>There&rsquo;s nothing more annoying than playing a competitive game on a monitor that lags. When every second matters, you need something that can keep up with the flow. That&rsquo;s where gaming monitors come in. Their high refresh rates are designed to make your game look as smooth as possible. Check out the options below.</p>

<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-block faq-block"><h2 class="faq-block-title" id="faq"> FAQ </h2><hr class="block-horizotal-divider" /><div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-inner-block faq-save-block"><div class="faq-save-content"><span class="faq-rank">1.</span>
<h3 id="are-black-friday-monitor-deals-really-worth-it">Are Black Friday monitor deals really worth it?</h3>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-answer-block how-to-tip">
<p>Yes, absolutely, you can find some great deals on monitors during the week of Black Friday&mdash;as evidenced by the great deals in the article above. Mind you, in some tech categories&mdash;like say, wireless earbuds or phone chargers&mdash;you&rsquo;ll see discounts on off-brand gear we&rsquo;d never recommend. But when it comes to monitors, highly reputable brands like HP, Dell, Samsung and Lenovo will drop prices on great models. PCWorld strives to only recommend deals on solid monitors that are experiencing legitimate pricing drops. To this end, we look for models that have reached or fallen below their all-time-low prices.</p>
</div>
</div></div>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-inner-block faq-save-block"><div class="faq-save-content"><span class="faq-rank">2.</span>
<h3 id="are-black-friday-monitor-deals-lower-quality">Are Black Friday monitor deals lower quality?</h3>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-answer-block how-to-tip">
<p>No, there&rsquo;s no reason why the monitor deals you find during Black Friday should be lower quality&mdash;at least if you focus on the big-name manufacturers like Samsung, Philips, LG, Dell, HP, Lenovo and so on. It&rsquo;s true that some of the discounted monitors may be 2021 models, but there&rsquo;s nothing wrong with that. Monitor tech moves rather slowly and there won&rsquo;t be major quality differences between 2021 and 2022 models. The important thing is to get a monitor at a legitimately lower price&mdash;and we have done the heavy lifting to curate those legit deals.</p>
</div>
</div></div>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-inner-block faq-save-block"><div class="faq-save-content"><span class="faq-rank">3.</span>
<h3 id="what-should-i-look-for-in-a-black-friday-monitor">What should I look for in a Black Friday monitor?</h3>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-answer-block how-to-tip">
<p>Ah, we&rsquo;ve arrived at the question of the hour.</p>



<p>Let&rsquo;s first talk about refresh rate, which is important if you&rsquo;re looking for a gaming monitor. The refresh rate is how fast a monitor can redraw the image on its screen. The faster the refresh rate, the smoother your visuals will look. For competitive first-person shooters, we&rsquo;d recommend 120Hz as the minimum rate. Anything higher is good enough for the eSports realm.</p>



<p>Resolution is another important feature to consider. Much like the refresh rate, the higher the number, the better. We&rsquo;re talking about the quality of images and video here. 1080p is the bare minimum for most&nbsp;monitors. However, if you&rsquo;re a video editor, bumping the resolution up to 4K makes a massive difference, as it allows you to see more detail.</p>



<p>The final thing is the screen size. 27 inches is the most common and a good size for a home office. For gaming monitors, 24 or 27 inches is best. Sometimes a larger screen causes eye strain and if you&rsquo;re going to be staring at one for hours, it&rsquo;s better to go a bit smaller. For 4K monitors, 32-inches is a good option, as it gives you quite a bit of screen to work with.</p>
</div>
</div></div>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-inner-block faq-save-block"><div class="faq-save-content"><span class="faq-rank">4.</span>
<h3 id="where-can-i-find-the-highest-rated-monitors">Where can I find the highest rated monitors?</h3>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-answer-block how-to-tip">
<p>PCWorld&nbsp;reviews&nbsp;new monitors every month. So, if you want to see the models we&rsquo;ve rated the highest, check out our rankings for the&nbsp;<a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/811315/best-monitors-2.html">best monitors of 2022</a>. We also have more granular picks on the&nbsp;<a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/813301/best-gaming-monitors.html">best gaming monitors</a>, as well as the&nbsp;<a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/813361/best-4k-monitors.html">best 4K monitors for desktop workstations</a>. Come Black Friday, a lot of our top picks may be on sale, so don&rsquo;t limit your shopping only to the deals we&rsquo;ve called out above.</p>
</div>
</div></div>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-inner-block faq-save-block"><div class="faq-save-content"><span class="faq-rank">5.</span>
<h3 id="what-black-friday-retailers-should-i-check-out">What Black Friday retailers should I check out?</h3>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-answer-block how-to-tip">
<p>Amazon&rsquo;s going to have a slew of awesome deals. That&rsquo;s a given. However, for monitors, you should definitely peruse the main pages of HP, Dell and Lenovo. Personally, I find myself going directly to the manufacturers more often than not. You can also widen your net and scope out other online retailers like Best Buy and Newegg.</p>
</div>
</div></div>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-inner-block faq-save-block"><div class="faq-save-content"><span class="faq-rank">6.</span>
<h3 id="when-is-black-friday-2022">When is Black Friday 2022?</h3>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-answer-block how-to-tip">
<p>Black Friday is on Friday, Nov 25th 2022. If you consider yourself an avid deals hunter, we&rsquo;d suggest going online in the early hours to take advantage of the best deals. Deals tend to change and expire at a breakneck pace.</p>
</div>
</div></div>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-inner-block faq-save-block"><div class="faq-save-content"><span class="faq-rank">7.</span>
<h3 id="when-is-cyber-monday-2022">When is Cyber Monday 2022?</h3>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-answer-block how-to-tip">
<p>Cyber Monday is on Monday, Nov 28th 2022. For the best deals, we&rsquo;d recommend logging on at midnight, as stock tends to deplete rather quickly.</p>
</div>
</div></div>

<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-block faq-block"><h2 class="faq-block-title" id="faq"> FAQ </h2><hr class="block-horizotal-divider" /><div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-inner-block faq-save-block"><div class="faq-save-content"><span class="faq-rank">1.</span>
<h3 id="are-best-buys-black-friday-deals-actually-good">Are Best Buy&rsquo;s Black Friday deals actually good?</h3>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-answer-block how-to-tip">
<p>Some of Best Buy&rsquo;s deals are quite good! The tricky part is knowing which are the best deals and which aren&rsquo;t, since major retailers generally put a bunch of stuff on sale. Not all items are solid products, and not all discounts are solid price drops. That&rsquo;s where we come in&mdash;we sift through the sales to find good gear at truly great prices.</p>
</div>
</div></div>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-inner-block faq-save-block"><div class="faq-save-content"><span class="faq-rank">2.</span>
<h3 id="are-any-of-the-black-friday-deals-at-best-buy-lower-quality">Are any of the Black Friday deals at Best Buy lower quality?</h3>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-answer-block how-to-tip">
<p>It depends on the product category, but usually the practice of creating special models for specific periods is limited to TVs. For most everything else, the items are the same as you&rsquo;d find throughout the rest of the year. But again, that&rsquo;s what we&rsquo;re here for: We&rsquo;ve carefully examined the specs and overall value of the deals listed above, so you can shop with more confidence and less hassle.</p>
</div>
</div></div>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-inner-block faq-save-block"><div class="faq-save-content"><span class="faq-rank">3.</span>
<h3 id="what-kind-of-black-friday-deals-can-i-expect-at-best-buy">What kind of Black Friday deals can I expect at Best Buy?</h3>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-answer-block how-to-tip">
<p>Best Buy discounts most product categories during Black Friday. During the rest of the year, Best Buy&rsquo;s sales trend more modest than other retailers&mdash;as one of the few stores that still has physical locations, it can&rsquo;t be as aggressive in slashing prices. But during November, it wades much deeper into the fray. The trick is to know which items are also sold by other vendors: For common items like headphones, Amazon Echo speakers, Fitbits, and other consumer electronics, any good discount should match or even undercut a rival store.</p>
</div>
</div></div>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-inner-block faq-save-block"><div class="faq-save-content"><span class="faq-rank">4.</span>
<h3 id="is-there-any-advantage-to-shopping-at-best-buy-during-black-friday">Is there any advantage to shopping at Best Buy during Black Friday?</h3>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-answer-block how-to-tip">
<p>For people who don&rsquo;t have Amazon Prime subscriptions or can&rsquo;t trust deliveries to arrive safely, Best Buy lets you get in on Black Friday discounts in a convenient way. You can order online and then opt to pick up in store. It can also be easier to make returns, since Best Buy will accept those in store as well, too. But the answer to this question is dependent on where you live and what&rsquo;s easiest for you.</p>
</div>
</div></div>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-inner-block faq-save-block"><div class="faq-save-content"><span class="faq-rank">5.</span>
<h3>When is Black Friday this year?<br /></h3>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-answer-block how-to-tip">
<p>Strictly speaking, Black Friday falls on November 25, 2022. But in reality already started earlier this month, allowing you to pick up great deals well before the official day.</p>
</div>
</div></div>
</div>

It has faster performance than rival options like the Samsung 980 Pro and Crucial P5 Plus. However, if cost is an issue, the 1TB Crucial P5 Plus deal at Best Buy, which includes a low-profile heatsink, is your cheapest option.</p>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-block faq-block"><h2 class="faq-block-title" id="faq"> FAQ </h2><hr class="block-horizotal-divider" /><div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-inner-block faq-save-block"><div class="faq-save-content"><span class="faq-rank">1.</span>
<h3 id="are-black-friday-ssd-deals-worth-it">Are Black Friday SSD deals worth it?</h3>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-answer-block how-to-tip">
<p>Absolutely yes. You can save a significant amount of money (sometimes hundreds of dollars on a high capacity drive) during the big Black Friday sale period. The trick is to know what&rsquo;s a good deal, and what&rsquo;s not. That&rsquo;s where we come in: We&rsquo;ve scoured reputable online retailers, looking for demonstrably good hardware at legitimately good discounts.</p>
</div>
</div></div>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-inner-block faq-save-block"><div class="faq-save-content"><span class="faq-rank">2.</span>
<h3 id="how-much-are-ssds-on-black-friday">How much are SSDs on Black Friday?</h3>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-answer-block how-to-tip">
<p>Prices depend on the usual street or retail price of the SSD model&mdash;so type of drive, its capacity, and its speed are all factors. Generally, expect to pay about $70 for a good 1TB SATA or NVMe Gen 3 drive, and $100 for a 1TB NVMe Gen 4 drive. But the easier guideline to just look for discounts of at least 20 percent or more.</p>
</div>
</div></div>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-inner-block faq-save-block"><div class="faq-save-content"><span class="faq-rank">3.</span>
<h3 id="are-black-friday-ssds-lower-quality">Are Black Friday SSDs lower quality?</h3>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-answer-block how-to-tip">
<p>Nope! Unlike other products, SSD vendors don&rsquo;t produce special models for sale periods like Black Friday. These are the same models you&rsquo;d find on a retail shelf or available on a website throughout the rest of the year.</p>
</div>
</div></div>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-inner-block faq-save-block"><div class="faq-save-content"><span class="faq-rank">4.</span>
<h3 id="what-should-i-look-for-in-a-black-friday-ssd-deal">What should I look for in a Black Friday SSD deal?</h3>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-answer-block how-to-tip">
<p>The best Black Friday deals drop prices on SSDs from reliable brands. A good discount starts around 15 to 20 percent&mdash;and a great deal will be 30 percent or more. Typically, the bigger bargains are higher-capacity SSDs (2TB or higher).</p>



<p>For the specific brands to watch, stick with known names like Samsung, Crucial, SK Hynix, Western Digital, Kingston, and Sabrent. TeamGroup and PNY are also options. The further afield you go, the more likely you&rsquo;ll end up with underperforming (aka slow) drives.</p>



<p>Pay attention to the model, as well. You can often find multiple drives from a single vendor on sale. The usual sweet spots are discounts on high-performing drives rarely on sale and steep price cuts on budget models. This year we should finally see sizable reductions on high-capacity drives (2TB and up), too.</p>
</div>
</div></div>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-inner-block faq-save-block"><div class="faq-save-content"><span class="faq-rank">5.</span>
<h3 id="what-kind-of-ssd-should-i-buy">What kind of SSD should I buy?</h3>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-answer-block how-to-tip">
<p>This is the big question. If you&rsquo;re on a budget, and have a laptop or a PC that has space for a 2.5-inch drive, a humble SATA SSD will already feel like a lightning fast upgrade from a spinning-platter (HDD) boot drive. (SATA SSDs also exist in the gumstick M.2 size, but this year&rsquo;s best sales for that form factor are the faster NVMe SSDs.)</p>



<p>For those trying to decide between NVMe Gen 3 and NVMe Gen 4 drives, most people can buy a Gen 3 drive with a light heart. Unless you&rsquo;re doing frequent large file transfers (think many GB at a time), you&rsquo;ll get a notable boost in performance over a SATA drive without spending a ton of extra cash. If you&rsquo;re building a system or buying for the very long haul, though, a Gen 4 drive is a good investment. File sizes will only climb over time for game installs, videos, and photos.</p>



<p>Still having trouble deciding? You can check out <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/394015/what-type-of-ssd-should-you-buy.html">our guide on choosing an SSD</a> for more details about each type of solid-state drive.</p>
</div>
</div></div>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-inner-block faq-save-block"><div class="faq-save-content"><span class="faq-rank">6.</span>
<h3 id="which-ssds-does-pcworld-rate-the-highest">Which SSDs does PCWorld rate the highest?</h3>



<div class="wp-block-idg-base-theme-faq-answer-block how-to-tip">
<p>PCWorld tests and reviews new SSDs every month, so if you&rsquo;re looking to see what we recommend without regard to deal prices, check our <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/407542/best-ssds.html">rankings of the best SSDs of 2022</a>. But it&rsquo;s not an either/or situation: Some of our top picks are on sale right now!</p>
</div>
</div></div>
</div>
Solid-State Drives</div>
